  - listitem:
    - strong: What is the main premise of the Gate Control Theory of pain?
    - text: "Your answer: No answer Correct answer: Pain signals can be blocked at the spinal cord level by non-painful input Explanation: The Gate Control Theory suggests that non-painful input can block or reduce the perception of pain signals at the spinal cord level. More Info: The Gate Control Theory, developed by Melzack and Wall in the 1960s, proposes that pain is not a direct result of activation of pain receptors, but rather it is modulated by a gating mechanism in the spinal cord. Non-painful stimuli, like pressure or touch, can activate larger nerve fibers (A-beta), which in turn inhibit pain transmission from smaller pain fibers (A-delta and C fibers). This theory helps explain why rubbing an area after injury can decrease discomfort."
  - listitem:
